  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/714490-i-m-currently-working-on-transgressive">I&#39;m currently working on transgressive forms of gender, basically all forms that don&#39;t fit the binary distinction male/female. The aim is to construct a literary analysis, meaning that I will analyse novels in which genderqueer characters or issues are at stake. I want to focus on 21st-century novels so my question is if anyone can recommend me any good literary, genderqueer novels written in or after the year 2000?</a>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/737146-isn-t-the-withholding-of-the-gender-of-the">Isn&#39;t the withholding of the gender of the narrator the most important part of the book? By withholding that critical piece of information, I had to judge the actions and decisions on their own merits rather than through the lens of gender expectations, which would make some decisions better or worse depending upon if a man or woman made them.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_737146'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F15054.Written_on_the_Body">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/737146-isn-t-the-withholding-of-the-gender-of-the">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/737146-isn-t-the-withholding-of-the-gender-of-the">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/10298127-anne"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1530315692i/10298127._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/10298127-anne">Anne</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I don't know if it's the most important part, but it is very important. Exactly, as a reader you have to judge actions and decisions free from gender <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't know if it's the most important part, but it is very important. Exactly, as a reader you have to judge actions and decisions free from gender expectations. But what's more, I noticed that it just emphasised for me how arbitrary gender norms are, and how crazy it is that this sediment of opinions on behaviour influences our lives and our image of ourselves and others so much. <br /><br />I think the other important thread is the narrator's views on romantic love. The attitude towards it is pretty similar: why follow culture-bound rules on love if they don't make you as an individual happy? The book is not without its faults, but it does invite the reader to investigate whether aspects of culture can be artificial and arbitrary, and I think that is very valuable.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2658186459" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2658186459" />
    <a title="Candi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3639005-candi"><img alt="Candi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585187464p2/3639005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2658186459?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candi" href="/user/show/3639005-candi">Candi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18886278-written-on-the-body">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=contemporary-literary">contemporary-literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2658186459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3009438416298339909"><i>“The pads of your fingers have become printing blocks, you tap a message on to my skin, tap meaning into my body. Your morse code interferes with my heart beat. I had a steady heart before I met you, I relied upon it, it had seen active service and grown strong. Now you alter its pace with your own rhythm, you play upon me, drumming me taut.”</i><br/><br/>I got completely lost in this book, in a good way. I was wholly wrapped up in the writing, basking in the beauty of the prose. I’ve not read a lot of Jeanet</span>
  <span id="freeText3009438416298339909" style="display:none"><i>“The pads of your fingers have become printing blocks, you tap a message on to my skin, tap meaning into my body. Your morse code interferes with my heart beat. I had a steady heart before I met you, I relied upon it, it had seen active service and grown strong. Now you alter its pace with your own rhythm, you play upon me, drumming me taut.”</i><br /><br />I got completely lost in this book, in a good way. I was wholly wrapped up in the writing, basking in the beauty of the prose. I’ve not read a lot of Jeanette Winterson yet, but what I know so far is that she is like a composer of music. Her words are a song that serenades the listener; this novel an exquisite ballad. When the breathless hush blankets the crowd after the conclusion of the piece, my greatest desire is to experience it all over again. <br /><br /><i>“I’ve tried to get you out of my head but I can’t seem to get you out of my flesh. I think about your body day and night. When I try to read it’s you I’m reading. When I sit down to eat it’s you I’m eating. When he touches me I think about you.”</i><br /><br />The skin of this story is an affair between a married woman and a narrator whose gender remains unnamed throughout. The flesh is the grand passion between these two, the sensuality of two bodies joined together. At the pit or core you will find unconditional, selfless love. <br /><br /><i>“I don’t want to be your sport nor you to be mine. I don’t want to punch you for the pleasure of it, tangling the clear lines that bind us, forcing you to your knees, dragging you up again. The public face of a life in chaos. I want the hoop around our hearts to be a guide not a terror.”</i><br /><br />The middle section reads like a poem about the various landscapes of a lover’s body. The beautiful verses still resound in my head. I was ready to forgive Winterson for overlooking a plot to her novel, until I realized there in fact was one. Beneath all that seductive style, a story is revealed. It shook me up and then crushed me. I loved it. <br /><br /><i>“Many waters cannot quench love, neither can floods drown it. What then kills love? Only this: Neglect. Not to see you when you stand before me. Not to think of you in the little things. Not to make the road wide for you, the table spread for you. To choose you out of habit not desire, to pass the flower seller without a thought.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3009438416298339909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16318939?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/940777-anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16318939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer383588374984038718">You know how it is when your friends fall madly in love with someone (a new girlfriend), or something (Guitar Hero, Battlestar Galactica), and wear you out during the honeymoon phase babbling on about his/her/its awesomeness, sometimes in excruciating detail? If you're not in a similar situation, or worse, wish you were, it's damn near unendurable. <br/><br/>For God's sake, don't read this book unless you can stand to read about sheer, uninhibited passion, often in graphic detail. The pointedly genderless</span>
  <span id="freeText383588374984038718" style="display:none">You know how it is when your friends fall madly in love with someone (a new girlfriend), or something (Guitar Hero, Battlestar Galactica), and wear you out during the honeymoon phase babbling on about his/her/its awesomeness, sometimes in excruciating detail? If you're not in a similar situation, or worse, wish you were, it's damn near unendurable. <br /><br />For God's sake, don't read this book unless you can stand to read about sheer, uninhibited passion, often in graphic detail. The pointedly genderless narrator, having wandered through the nooks and crannies of various male and female lovers, falls head over heels for Louise, and, when foolish enough to lose her, spends roughly a third of the book singing paeans to her entire body. It's Winterson at her most self-indulgent, but in this case, her enthusiasm is well-suited to its subject. If you've ever been stupid in love with someone, you can sympathize with narrator x, and appreciate Winterson's matchless style. <br /><br />Definitely a book you've got to be in the right mood for, by which I mean if you're in an unhappy relationship or you aren't seeing anyone and wish you were, or God help you just got dumped, stay the hell away. If you're bazonkers about someone right now or otherwise don't mind, read this, it will thrill you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="383588374984038718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_746694411" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/746694411" />
    <a title="Dolors" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18383778-dolors"><img alt="Dolors" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502350013p2/18383778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/746694411?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dolors" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dolors" href="/user/show/18383778-dolors">Dolors</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/21853868-written-on-the-body">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those sick with love</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18383778-dolors?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer746694411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11329506512937863296">A genderless narrator leafs through past affairs with men and women, contrasting them with his/her present relationship with Louise, a married woman. <br/>What I most admired about Winterson’s approach to this tragic romance is the naturalness with which she approaches homosexual and bisexual relationships, which makes a case for the idea that gender is but a sociocultural construct, a concept that certainly shouldn’t define the traits of any relationship, or in this case, of the narrator, who seems </span>
  <span id="freeText11329506512937863296" style="display:none">A genderless narrator leafs through past affairs with men and women, contrasting them with his/her present relationship with Louise, a married woman. <br />What I most admired about Winterson’s approach to this tragic romance is the naturalness with which she approaches homosexual and bisexual relationships, which makes a case for the idea that gender is but a sociocultural construct, a concept that certainly shouldn’t define the traits of any relationship, or in this case, of the narrator, who seems humane and very plausible even without attributed male or female stereotyped features. <br /><br />Another aspect that I found remarkable was the middle section of the novel, which is devoted to create an ode to the body of the lover, some sort of poetic exaltation about every inch of the beloved’s flesh, even her cells and tissues, presenting them as virgin territories to discover, to bask in, and finally, to conquer.<br /><br />Why my temperate response, then? *spoilers ahead*<br />I thought the story didn’t need the element of a terminal illness to make a point about loving and losing the person who finally teaches us selfless love. <br />In addition, the narrator’s point of view is contemplative and locked within his/her version of events, and even though the novel is replete with memorable quotes, I was a bit overwhelmed with the exuberant stylistic resources employed to draw the narrator’s inner world. <br />The ending is open to interpretation, and that gave the escalating pace of the last pages an anti-climatic closure, and I couldn’t help but compare it with Baldwin’s <i>“Giovanni’s Room”</i>, a novel that deals with similar issues and offers a broader and, in my opinion, subtler but more incisive vision of love, loss and grief without employing sentimentality as the final trick. Giovanni’s empty room shook me a thousand times more than Winterson’s veneration of a lover’s body.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11329506512937863296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_977328543" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/977328543" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480492067p2/32532774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977328543?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=jeanette-winterson">jeanette-winterson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=1001-books-to-read-before-you-die">1001-books-to-read-before-you-die</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977328543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer426842954034685470">It is hard to review Jeanette Winterson. <br/><br/>Every single one of her short novels is a work of art, beautiful and painfully true while magically exploring the limits of reality.<br/><br/>I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15047.The_Passion' title='The Passion by Jeanette Winterson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Passion</a> and thought I would not like it, because I don't do historical fiction. It was breath-taking, unbelievable, eye-opening. The recurring theme accompanies me ever since: "Somewhere between fear and sex, passion is."<br/><br/>I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15050.Sexing_the_Cherry' title='Sexing the Cherry by Jeanette Winterson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sexing the Cherry</a> and thought I could not possibly like it more, because <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15047.The_Passion' title='The Passion by Jeanette Winterson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Passion</a> mad</span>
  <span id="freeText426842954034685470" style="display:none">It is hard to review Jeanette Winterson. <br /><br />Every single one of her short novels is a work of art, beautiful and painfully true while magically exploring the limits of reality.<br /><br />I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15047.The_Passion" title="The Passion by Jeanette Winterson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Passion</a> and thought I would not like it, because I don't do historical fiction. It was breath-taking, unbelievable, eye-opening. The recurring theme accompanies me ever since: "Somewhere between fear and sex, passion is."<br /><br />I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15050.Sexing_the_Cherry" title="Sexing the Cherry by Jeanette Winterson" rel="nofollow noopener">Sexing the Cherry</a> and thought I could not possibly like it more, because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15047.The_Passion" title="The Passion by Jeanette Winterson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Passion</a> made such an impression on me, and I was blown away. Pure magic! <br /><br />To evaluate the other novels by her I have read, I have to reread them, because the language and the plot are always so carefully interlinked, it is hard to explain the massive effect of her words from memory. This weekend I started the process with Written On The Body, which I remembered only vaguely, thinking I had liked it despite not being fond of love stories. And I swear, the book now is tattooed, written into my soul. Picking up the recurring themes of desire, passion, and deceit, it explores the nature of love against all odds, against rational thinking, against one's own body.<br /><br />The main idea is to describe the complete surrender a person experiences when he or she loves unconditionally, and how that leaves traces, not only on the soul, but on the body itself. The intensity of the feeling is engraved on the body.<br /><br />It is shockingly honest in its approach to adultery, deceit, and the randomness of love. Love is all-consuming, but rarely something purely beautiful. Its start can be a banality, the door to love opened by accident:<br /><br />“Her butler opened it for her. His name was Boredom. She said, 'Boredom, fetch me a plaything.' He said 'Very good ma'am,' and putting on his white gloves so that fingerprints would not show he tapped at my heart and I thought he said his name was Love.” <br /><br />As always, Winterson mixes deep feelings with sarcastic comical effects:<br /><br />"It would have been good to have lain down there and made love under the moon, but the truth is that, outside of the movies and the Country and Western songs, the outdoors is an itchy business."<br /><br />The nameless main character plays many different relationship roles over the course of the story. The adventurous affair, the unhappy love, the comfortable stable partnership:<br /><br />"I was rigorous, hard working and... and... what was that word with B again?<br />You're bored, my friend said.<br />I protested with all the fervour of a teetotaller caught glancing at the bottle. I was content. I had settled."<br /><br />And then the big LOVE strikes, the one that goes straight through the body and soul and leaves the character marked for life, literally. No rational thinking helps:<br /><br />"Wisdom says forget. The body howls."<br /><br />In the end, there is something like a happy ending, a beginning as well, a couple of human beings let loose in the open fields.<br /><br />This is a Winterson, through and through, every word weighing heavily, every emotion raw. <br /><br />Read it if you can bear to have the pain of love written on your body.</span>
  <a data-text-id="426842954034685470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1832528612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1832528612" />
    <a title="Cecily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily"><img alt="Cecily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480285828p2/1199525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1832528612?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecily" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily">Cecily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=sexuality-gender-lgbtq">sexuality-gender-lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=miscellaneous-fiction">miscellaneous-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=death-bereavement">death-bereavement</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1832528612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9436778726347068283">On the surface, this is a sensual, reflective, and sometimes humorous recollection of the narrator’s loves won and lost, compared with the current one. Unwelcome news triggers a difficult choice, with huge ramifications. It was made with love, but was it the right decision, and did the narrator even have the right to make it? It’s a curious amalgam of styles, yet unmistakably Winterson, including a set of short, more abstract sections, and the fact the bisexual narrator’s gender is unspecified.<br/> </span>
  <span id="freeText9436778726347068283" style="display:none">On the surface, this is a sensual, reflective, and sometimes humorous recollection of the narrator’s loves won and lost, compared with the current one. Unwelcome news triggers a difficult choice, with huge ramifications. It was made with love, but was it the right decision, and did the narrator even have the right to make it? It’s a curious amalgam of styles, yet unmistakably Winterson, including a set of short, more abstract sections, and the fact the bisexual narrator’s gender is unspecified.<br> <br>But peel back the gilt and what’s beneath is not so straightforward. All the best literature has a unique message for every reader, on each encounter. Gilt reflects: what spoke to me is not what you will hear and respond to. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554646895i/27328043.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>Antique mirror</i> (<a href="https://homeguides.sfgate.com/identify-antique-mirrors-89891.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.)<br><br>I found this shockingly, painfully good. I knew it was about relationships and was ambiguous about gender, but I was unprepared for the raw dissection of loss. It punched hard, but was shot through with love. Definitely the right book at the right time for me. <br><br>“<i>
  <b>Why is the measure of love loss?</b>
</i>”<br><br>The opening line, repeated later, brought tears. It’s the converse of my recent experience of grief as the price of love - love with nowhere to go. But nevertheless, and without question, “Love is worth it”.<br><br>"<i>You don't get over it because 'it' is the person you loved.</i>"<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554646895i/27328044._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: My father’s keys, his writing instantly recognisable from just four letters.<br>“<i>No-one tells you in grief-counselling or books on loss what it will be like when you find part of the beloved unexpectedly.</i>”<br><br><b>Love is…</b><br><br>“<i>I went to church… I wanted the comfort of other people’s faith.</i>”<br><br>The Bible of her childhood infuses atheist Winterson’s writing, and this is no exception: phrases, ideas, and liturgical repetition and rhythm. Here, it’s most obvious in how the “emotional nomad” writes about love:<br><br>“<i>Love demands expression. It will not stay still, stay silent, be good, be modest, be seen and not heard, no.</i>”<br>and<br>“<i>No-one can legislate love; it cannot be given orders or cajoled into service. Love belongs to itself, deaf to pleading and unmoved by violence. Love is not something you can negotiate. Love is the one thing stronger than desire and the only proper reason to resist temptation.</i>”<br><br>From 1 Corinthians 13, v4-8 (NIV):<br>“<i>Love is patient, love is kind. It does not envy, it does not boast, it is not proud. It does not dishonor others, it is not self-seeking, it is not easily angered, it keeps no record of wrongs. Love does not delight in evil but rejoices with the truth. It always protects, always trusts, always hopes, always perseveres. Love never fails.</i>” <br><br>But I don’t think the Bible is right: love <b>can</b> fail:<br>“<i>What then kills love? Only this: neglect.</i>”<br><br>The other message, from way back in 1992, is that gender doesn’t matter; there is no question or hand-wringing; it’s not relevant to the story. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554647314i/27328052.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Image</b>: <i>“Love is love” in current parlance.</i> (<a href="https://www.shutterstock.com/image-vector/gay-love-1101422276" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.)<br><br><b>Marriage</b><br><br>“<i>Is happiness always a compromise?</i>”<br>“<i>Contentment… are you sure it’s not an absence of feeling?</i>”<br><br>In my teens, I remember my father quoting (allegedly) Prince Philip: “Marriage is the highest form of prostitution”. There is truth in that, touched on repeatedly here. We all exchange things for sex and love: our motives are mixed and rarely pure. And the promises of marriage can be hard to keep.<br><br>“<i>Marriage is the flimsiest weapon against desire.</i>”<br>“<i>Cheating is easy… To borrow against the trust someone has placed in you costs nothing <b>at first</b>.</i>”<br><br><b>The Translator, Translated</b><br><br>“<i>Articulacy of the fingers… signing on the body body longing.</i>”<br>“<i>Your flesh is my flesh. You deciphered me and now I am plain to read.</i>”<br><br>The narrator is a translator (there are many references to great literature, as usual for Winterson), but better in abstract than with those they love, let alone themself.<br><br>“<i>Written on the body is a secret code only visible in certain lights… In places the palimpsest is so heavily worked that the letters feel like Braille… I didn’t know that Louse would have reading hands. She has translated me into her own book.</i>”<br><br><b>Bio-anatomical Prose Poetry</b><br><br>“<i>I know the stigmata of presumption.</i>”<br><br>There are no chapters, but two-thirds through, there are four short sections that defy easy description: semi-abstract musings on cells, skin, skeleton, and “special senses”, as the narrator agonises over anticipatory loss in a profound and sensual way.<br><br>“<i>To remember you it’s my own body I touch.</i>”<br><br><b>Ending</b><br><br>“<i>Is this the proper ending? If not the proper then the inevitable?</i>”<br><br>As I approached the end, I was nervous: I wasn’t sure what a happy ending would be, but knew I didn't want one. I need not have feared. It is everything and nothing - interpret as you like. I could quote the whole closing paragraph, without fear of spoilers.<br><br>In her brilliant autobiography, <b>Why be Happy when you Could be Normal?</b> (see my review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332816058" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>), Winterson categorises three types of ending: revenge, tragedy and forgiveness. Both books contain all three.<br><br><b>Other Quotes</b><br><br>Memory of Love<br>•	“How easy is it to destroy the past and how difficult to forget it?”<br>•	“Wisdom says forget. The body howls.”<br>•	“I’ve tried to get you out of my head but I can’t seem to get you out of my flesh.”<br>•	“I don’t want to be reminded of you, I want you.”<br>•	“The power of memory is such that it can lift reality for a time.”<br><br>Relationships and Fallout<br>•	“I used to think of marriage as a plate-glass window just begging for a brick.”<br>•	“Odd that marriage, a public display and free to all, gives way to that most secret of liaisons, an adulterous affair.”<br>•	“I had to keep my heart to myself in case I infected somebody” with “emotional clap”.<br>•	“You never give away your heart; you lend it from time to time.”<br>•	“I had no dreams to possess you - but I wanted you to possess me.”<br>•	“With old friends… you know one another as well as lovers do and you have less to pretend about” - so you’re more likely to be honest. <br><br>Dry Humour<br>•	“The ultimate act of selfishness; a woman who put herself first.”<br>•	“Her husband lies over her like a tarpaulin.”<br>•	“The women wore their jewellery like medals… a palimpsest of love-affairs” on show at the opera.<br>•	 “I’d run my hands over her padded flesh with all the enthusiasm of a second-hand sofa dealer.”<br>•	“They considered themselves to be Australian aristocracy, that is, they were descended from convicts.”<br>•	“She had a steady hand but she like to spill. It made work for her daughter.”<br><br>Other<br>•	“What you risk reveals what you value.”<br>•	“People usually know exactly why they are happy. They very rarely know why they are miserable.”<br><br>Winterson is queen of the extended metaphor. This is one of many (others include maps, animals, jigsaws):<br>“<i>When she lifted the soup spoon to her lips how I longed to be that innocent piece of stainless steel… Let me be diced carrot, vermicelli, just so that you will take me in your mouth. I envied the French stick. I watched her break and butter each piece, soak it slowly in her bowl, let it float, grow heavy and fat, sink under the deep red weight and then be resurrected to the glorious pleasure of her teeth… I will taste you if only through your cooking.</i>”</span>
  <a data-text-id="9436778726347068283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36555254-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536187488p2/36555254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2069401980?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/36555254-robin">Robin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=1001-before-you-die">1001-before-you-die</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=english">english</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2069401980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7431072125190597356">Jeanette Winterson impressed me last year when I read her magical tale of historical fiction, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15047.The_Passion' title='The Passion by Jeanette Winterson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Passion</a>. Her poetic, interior style really resonated with me. Her work lays deep in the physical heart while also sparkling on an ethereal plane.<br/><br/>This book knocked me out. Her sheer artistry had me in admiration. A bit slack-jawed, actually. For example, the main character is not only nameless (I've seen that before) but is an 'every-person': Winterson doesn't tell us if they are male or female. Quit</span>
  <span id="freeText7431072125190597356" style="display:none">Jeanette Winterson impressed me last year when I read her magical tale of historical fiction, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15047.The_Passion" title="The Passion by Jeanette Winterson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Passion</a>. Her poetic, interior style really resonated with me. Her work lays deep in the physical heart while also sparkling on an ethereal plane.<br /><br />This book knocked me out. Her sheer artistry had me in admiration. A bit slack-jawed, actually. For example, the main character is not only nameless (I've seen that before) but is an 'every-person': Winterson doesn't tell us if they are male or female. Quite a feat for a book replete with sensual body worshipping between lovers. The effect is powerful - the reader can put themselves in the place of the narrator, or insert whatever gender they see, it being secondary to the train wreck of LOVE that takes centre stage.<br /><br />Our main character has fallen in love with a woman, who is married to a man. The first part of this book is about their affair. Brace yourself. It is full of scalding truths about love, marriage and infidelity. There is much talk about love, and not all of it is corsets, sunsets and long stemmed roses. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Marriage is the flimsiest weapon against desire. You may as well take a pop-gun to a python.</b>
</i> <br /><br />The next part of the book is an anatomical ode to the body of the beloved. The skin, the bones, the cavities, the senses, they have affected the narrator in a manner just as profound as any other quality that inspires love. It's hard to know whether it's love that imprints on the body, or the body that sears its own tattoo on the soul of the person who loves them. Perhaps it is both.<br /><br />It is poetic, lyrical, and philosophical, but there's just the right amount of story to carry you along to the end, which, incidentally, I thought was perfect. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Nail me to you. I will ride you like a nightmare. You are the winged horse Pegasus who would not be saddled.</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7431072125190597356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6404668?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evan" href="/user/show/216337-evan">Evan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who loves love</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6404668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10561395372341914108">I was reading thru some of the reviews for this book. I'll just say that it's beautifully written. This book moved me. I cried with about twenty pages to go. My heart expanded and ached a little bit. I felt for the narrator (who we have to guess woman or man?) and for Louise. I love the narrator. This book is about love, relationships, loss, and is a bit hope filled at the end. The opening sentence: Why is the measure of love loss? and the book takes you from there. I finished it in a day. Not a</span>
  <span id="freeText10561395372341914108" style="display:none">I was reading thru some of the reviews for this book. I'll just say that it's beautifully written. This book moved me. I cried with about twenty pages to go. My heart expanded and ached a little bit. I felt for the narrator (who we have to guess woman or man?) and for Louise. I love the narrator. This book is about love, relationships, loss, and is a bit hope filled at the end. The opening sentence: Why is the measure of love loss? and the book takes you from there. I finished it in a day. Not a lot of pages and would have finished it in just 3-4 hours had it not been for it's language lending itself to my own experiences in relationships and thoughts about love. One third of the way in I wanted to start over so I wouldn't be so near the end. At times I had to stop reading and go out and sit in the sun, put my feet in the grass, listen to the rustle of a tree in our backyard. I saw a hummingbird. A dragonfly. The reading of this book was competing with nature all day. Only when the day settled could I concentrate enough to finish it up. All in all, my life is richer for having read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10561395372341914108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_292134450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292134450" />
    <a title="Jenn(ifer)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/780933-jenn-ifer"><img alt="Jenn(ifer)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579713607p2/780933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292134450?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn(ifer)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn(ifer)" href="/user/show/780933-jenn-ifer">Jenn(ifer)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/780933-jenn-ifer?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/780933-jenn-ifer?shelf=xx">xx</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/780933-jenn-ifer?shelf=brits">brits</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/780933-jenn-ifer?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/780933-jenn-ifer?shelf=my-reviews-that-dont-suck">my-reviews-that-dont-suck</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292134450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1394283704833357800"><br/>****************************<br/><br/>Listen along (please): <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y7JPH-ZtZSw'>http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y7JPH-...</a><br/><br/>****************************<br/><br/>When you fall in love with someone, I mean really fall, you become obsessed with the things that are written on the body. The scar on her elbow from when she tripped over the curb, the chip in his tooth from when he fell from his skateboard… that tiny birthmark behind her knee. Each mark tells a story. Knowing the story brings you closer. The burn mark on her hand from when she </span>
  <span id="freeText1394283704833357800" style="display:none"><br />****************************<br /><br />Listen along (please): <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y7JPH-ZtZSw">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y7JPH-...</a><br /><br />****************************<br /><br />When you fall in love with someone, I mean really fall, you become obsessed with the things that are written on the body. The scar on her elbow from when she tripped over the curb, the chip in his tooth from when he fell from his skateboard… that tiny birthmark behind her knee. Each mark tells a story. Knowing the story brings you closer. The burn mark on her hand from when she touched the hot stove… the freckles that dot the small of his back and look like Orion… that little heart on her hip that few people know about… the fillings in his mouth that you scan with your tongue… So many things that happened before you met are imprinted on her body to form a thousand memories. As you begin a life together, you become a part of those stories. … you know every mole, every line, every new wrinkle, every gray hair. <br /><br />'Written on the Body' is a beautifully written and powerful story about all of the pleasure and pain of loving, the cruelty of not loving enough and everything in between. The narrator seems to be in love with being in love (<i>“I’m addicted to the first 6 months"</i>). You’re right there with her (him? It’s unclear) as she falls in:<br /><br /><i>“When she lifted the soup spoon to her lips how I longed to be that innocent piece of stainless steel. I would gladly have traded the blood in my body for half a pint of vegetable stock. Let me be diced carrot, vermicelli, just so that you will take me in your mouth."</i><br /><br />The way Winterson writes is breathtaking. So often love stories are trite and sugary and predictable. But I didn’t see this one coming. It was magical. Pure poetry.<br /><br />********<br />Addendum: I meant to appeal to anyone who has read this book, please, let's discuss the ending! I wasn't sure what to make of it.<br /></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review292134450">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2208426413?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Bookishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Bookishly" href="/user/show/28323108-bookishly">~Bookishly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=broke-my-heart">broke-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=erotica">erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=i-love-love-love">i-love-love-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2208426413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14417554410470554388">"Love demands expression. It will not stay still, stay silent, be good, be modest, be seen and not heard, no. It will break out in tongues of praise, the high note that smashes the glass and spills the liquid"<br/><br/>"Written on the body" is a captivating and beautifully written story of all the pleasure and in turn, the heartache, loving someone can cause. The way Winterson writes, is actually almost magical. Her words are almost like silk, but they are at the same time, so, so powerful.<br/><br/>I have to admit</span>
  <span id="freeText14417554410470554388" style="display:none">"Love demands expression. It will not stay still, stay silent, be good, be modest, be seen and not heard, no. It will break out in tongues of praise, the high note that smashes the glass and spills the liquid"<br /><br />"Written on the body" is a captivating and beautifully written story of all the pleasure and in turn, the heartache, loving someone can cause. The way Winterson writes, is actually almost magical. Her words are almost like silk, but they are at the same time, so, so powerful.<br /><br />I have to admit, this wouldn't have been a book I would have personally gone out and bought. My Mother insisted I read it, and I'm glad I did, as I had no idea what was coming. I didn't want this book to end. <br /><br />"Misery is a vacuum. A space without air, a suffocated dead place, the abode of the miserable."<br /><br />The writing had such a poetic feel to it, and this made it very moving for me. I felt very sad nearing the end of the book. I could almost feel the utter rawness that the narrator was going through. Regardless of whether the narrator is male or female, makes absolutely no difference to me. This book was beautiful, and made quite an impact on my poor, aching heart, which quite honestly, needs time to recover after this beautiful little number.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14417554410470554388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18153373450510636308">Her artistry makes my mouth drop open. The most poetic, passionate, erotic book, it sits on my shelf with Duras' The Lover and Rikki Ducornet's The Word Desire and Anne Carson's The Beauty of the Husband. But it could also be shelved with Proust's Swann's Way for the sensual cling of memory and Chekhov's Lady with the Lapdog for its sadness. The poetry of its prose is incomparable. A meditation on sensual life and the meaning of love. As Carson said, 'Beauty is what makes sex, sex." A lover of u</span>
  <span id="freeText18153373450510636308" style="display:none">Her artistry makes my mouth drop open. The most poetic, passionate, erotic book, it sits on my shelf with Duras' The Lover and Rikki Ducornet's The Word Desire and Anne Carson's The Beauty of the Husband. But it could also be shelved with Proust's Swann's Way for the sensual cling of memory and Chekhov's Lady with the Lapdog for its sadness. The poetry of its prose is incomparable. A meditation on sensual life and the meaning of love. As Carson said, 'Beauty is what makes sex, sex." A lover of undetermined gender describing a relationship with a married woman. And what a lover. What deft ability to capture our thoughts about love. Our, meaning the human being. For what is writing besides capturing thoughts that belong to all of us, so that we can recognize ourselves, undestand ourselves, and perhaps, each other. Every thoughtful book about love makes us better lovers, I think. It opens the gates of perception.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18886278-written-on-the-body">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to booksnpenguins by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/10675488-swaye">Swaye </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=ya-na-contemporaries">ya-na-contemporaries</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2235748242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14212504597465430400"><blockquote>
  <i>Can love have texture? It is palpable to me, the feeling between us, I weight it in my hands the way I weight your head in my hands. <br/>It gives me a loose-limbed confidence to know you'll be there. I'm expected.<br/>There's continuum. There's freedom.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><i>Written On The Body</i> is more than a book, more than a story, more than anything even remotely quantifiable. <br/>Written on the Body is an accurate study on the power of consequences, a retrospection on pure and unconditionate love, written with the passion </span>
  <span id="freeText14212504597465430400" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Can love have texture? It is palpable to me, the feeling between us, I weight it in my hands the way I weight your head in my hands. <br />It gives me a loose-limbed confidence to know you'll be there. I'm expected.<br />There's continuum. There's freedom.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><i>Written On The Body</i> is more than a book, more than a story, more than anything even remotely quantifiable. <br />Written on the Body is an accurate study on the power of consequences, a retrospection on pure and unconditionate love, written with the passion of a thousand broken dreams. <br />The way it deals with sickness and pain and betrayal, moving from prose to authentic poetry in the same sentence, is what gives this book its aching and mangled edges. What places it within hand's reach. <br />I love the writing style and its tones. It was less like reading facts and more like actually feeling them properly on and under my very own skin. <br />The caresses, the tears, the smells, the wrong choices. Everything that could leave a tiny bittersweet scar in my reader's heart, it did. <br />It helps that the narrating voice has no name and no gender. <br />They're a character so deep and wounded by their present and past that it's way too easy to slide into their shoes and pretend you're experiencing the biggest and warmest kind of love of all times. <br /><br />I'm in love with that ending. It's pure perfection. <br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Written on the body is a se red code only visible in certain lights.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br />First buddy-read of the year with my beautiful Swaye❤️<br />Thanks for recommending me such another beautiful gem and for sharing it with me. <br />I'll always trust your taste in books ;)</span>

<div id="review_2724041304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2724041304" />
    <a title="Hugh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32318315-hugh"><img alt="Hugh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466451007p2/32318315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2724041304?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hugh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hugh" href="/user/show/32318315-hugh">Hugh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099598275" href="/book/show/20872990-written-on-the-body">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32318315-hugh?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32318315-hugh?shelf=modern-lit">modern-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2724041304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15230340077240736181">An interesting, sometimes funny, moving meditation on love and loss. The narrator, a translator of Russian fiction, is never named and his/her gender is deliberately ambiguous - he/she describes relationships with a number of lovers, mostly female but some male. The first half is fairly light in tone, as he/she describes the various affairs leading up to and including the dominant one which forms the main theme of the story, with a married woman called Louise, whose husband Elgin is a cancer spe</span>
  <span id="freeText15230340077240736181" style="display:none">An interesting, sometimes funny, moving meditation on love and loss. The narrator, a translator of Russian fiction, is never named and his/her gender is deliberately ambiguous - he/she describes relationships with a number of lovers, mostly female but some male. The first half is fairly light in tone, as he/she describes the various affairs leading up to and including the dominant one which forms the main theme of the story, with a married woman called Louise, whose husband Elgin is a cancer specialist. Louise eventually decides to leave her husband.<br /><br />The tone shifts abrubtly about halfway through, as Elgin tells the narrator that Louise is suffering from a form of leukemia that gives her an expected 100 months to live, and maybe less if she does not agree to the treatment he prescribes, so the narrator breaks off their relationship to allow the treatment, moving away to a cottage in rural Yorkshire. The second half begins rather oddly, as the narrator writes tributes to her which largely consist of a litany of possible symptoms. The narrator starts to suspect that Elgin is not telling all he knows, and eventually discovers that he has been deceiving them, setting off on a fruitless search for Louise. So if the first part is mostly about love, lust, obsession and betrayal, the second is more dominated by loss and morbidity, though never without the occasional touch of humour. The whole has a quiet power that gradually accumulates, particularly towards the end.<br /><br />Thanks to the <b>Reading the 20th Century</b> group for choosing this one as a group read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15230340077240736181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_25575298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25575298" />
    <a title="Alan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/318068-alan"><img alt="Alan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350575041p2/318068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25575298?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alan" href="/user/show/318068-alan">Alan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/318068-alan?shelf=abandoned-because-blew">abandoned-because-blew</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25575298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10791243285085538121">I tried really hard to like Jeanette Winterson, because most of the women I respect think she is amazing. But I just think she is fumbling and kind of incompetent. And for me her charisma, great passion, and several devastating one-liners don't compensate for her imprecision, scattered incoherence, or the clamminess of her authorial 'I.'<br/><br/>Can't do it.<br/><br/>(Wait, don't leave! I like Anais Nin. Seriously...)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review25575298">
  <td colspan="2">

<span id="freeTextContainer3832079489742226048">I don't believe I've ever read anyone who writes quite like Jeanette Winterson. She writes with a kind of sensuality that leaps over the conventional, making it arousing and painfully sad at the same time. It is incredible how she has managed to write a book in which you know not even the gender of the main character, but you know their emotions as intimately as if they were your own. After a single reading of this book, it became one of my favorites; not because the story is tragic (and it is),</span>
  <span id="freeText3832079489742226048" style="display:none">I don't believe I've ever read anyone who writes quite like Jeanette Winterson. She writes with a kind of sensuality that leaps over the conventional, making it arousing and painfully sad at the same time. It is incredible how she has managed to write a book in which you know not even the gender of the main character, but you know their emotions as intimately as if they were your own. After a single reading of this book, it became one of my favorites; not because the story is tragic (and it is), and not because the characters are vibrant, warm, and real (and they are), but because it is rare and wonderful to find writing that is this advanced, rich, gorgeous, and relatable. <br /></span>

<div id="review_2736627289" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2736627289" />
    <a title="Roman Clodia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56111743-roman-clodia"><img alt="Roman Clodia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464021031p2/56111743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2736627289?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roman Clodia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roman Clodia" href="/user/show/56111743-roman-clodia">Roman Clodia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/16432972-written-on-the-body">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2736627289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12680041298621263775"><i>
  <blockquote>It is so terrifying, love</blockquote>
</i><br/>In less than 200 pages, Winterson has written something both light and profound, immensely intimate and yet somehow public, replete with humour and anguish, selfishness and care, and which moves from high comedy (wit, satire, absurdity) to something very moving. The writing is lush and sensuous, but always intelligent as connections are made via words and language to join ideas that don't traditionally belong together. <br/><br/>In lots of ways this is a story that has been do</span>
  <span id="freeText12680041298621263775" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>It is so terrifying, love</blockquote>
</i><br />In less than 200 pages, Winterson has written something both light and profound, immensely intimate and yet somehow public, replete with humour and anguish, selfishness and care, and which moves from high comedy (wit, satire, absurdity) to something very moving. The writing is lush and sensuous, but always intelligent as connections are made via words and language to join ideas that don't traditionally belong together. <br /><br />In lots of ways this is a story that has been done many, many times before: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the beloved partner dying of terminal cancer <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but it's a fine example of how a worn plot can be refreshed and renewed via writing and the unique perspective of a thoughtful, sensitive writer. Rest assured, there's no cheap melodrama here. <br /><br />The big 'thing' about this book (it was first published in 1993 - is it still a 'thing' in 2019?) is that the narrator's name and gender is never told to us: we know they've been a Lothario, a Casanova, a Don Juan (funny how there are no equivalents for women) in their past with both male and female lovers; we know that they're a translator who works in the British Library (when it was still housed in the British Museum - burst of nostalgia!) - and we know that they're now deeply, obsessively in love with Louise. Do we need to know more? I didn't. <br /><br />So this is a story about love, about how it encompasses both mind and body. But it's also a story about someone who knows the risks of love and doesn't want to go there... till they find themselves in too deep already. The first half is all about the narrator and their consciousness, and the movement of the novel is outwards from the narrator's interiority to that of Louise's physical interior with paeans to her bones, her muscles, her cells, her tissues. Only at the end of this journey can the narrator look back at their travels and realise that they have moved from a kind of selfishness masquerading as love to something that embraces the other, regardless of the effect on self. It's enthralling... and moving... and exquisitely done.<br /><br />The book opens with a question and I think it ends with one, too, though the latter isn't articulated: how do we know we love? The narrator has found their answer. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12680041298621263775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to El by: </span>
      The F-Word
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=20th-centurylit-late">20th-centurylit-late</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=1001-books-list">1001-books-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=hear-me-roar-and-gender">hear-me-roar-and-gender</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1933919942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6236027800872928945">This is the second book now that I've read by Jeanette Winterson and I just want to keep reading her. Her stories are familiar, as in I can recognize that each is written by Winterson, because she has a way with words that not many authors can manage even if they wanted to. It's distinctly Winterson, and that's refreshing.<br/><br/>In this book, we have a genderless narrator. What does that mean? The narrator may in fact have a gender, but the point is that we, as the readers, do not have any idea. Is the</span>
  <span id="freeText6236027800872928945" style="display:none">This is the second book now that I've read by Jeanette Winterson and I just want to keep reading her. Her stories are familiar, as in I can recognize that each is written by Winterson, because she has a way with words that not many authors can manage even if they wanted to. It's distinctly Winterson, and that's refreshing.<br /><br />In this book, we have a genderless narrator. What does that mean? The narrator may in fact have a gender, but the point is that we, as the readers, do not have any idea. Is the narrator male or female? Does it matter? And more importantly, <i>why do we care?</i> It's unsettling, still in this day and age, to not know from the start whose story we're reading. As the narrator details their sexual exploits with men and women, we are left still uncertain, and ultimately it doesn't even matter. It's a story of love and devotion, lust, the way our stories are imprinted on our lovers' bodies. I say Winterson was ahead of the curve here with this one, illustrating to readers that our stories are not based on our genders, but on the love we can provide to another and accept in return.<br /><br />It's quite beautiful, really.<br /><br />There's a bit in the middle that reads more like an anatomical guide than a novel, but even that is written in Winterson's exquisite prose.<br /><blockquote>"He made me shave off all my body hair and did the same to himself. He claimed it would increase sensation but it made me feel like a prisoner in a beehive."<br />(p143)</blockquote><br />So far with this book and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15055.Oranges_Are_Not_the_Only_Fruit" title="Oranges Are Not the Only Fruit by Jeanette Winterson" rel="nofollow noopener">Oranges Are Not the Only Fruit</a>, I find myself at a distance from Winterson's writing, even though I have liked it so much both times. It's more an appreciation, but there's an emotional distance I find to her writing, like I can't quite get inside of it, like I'm not ready, perhaps, or it's not meant for me. It's not that I feel excluded; I just find myself trying to reach depths in her writing that I don't think she means to be reached, and as much as I like it, I can't say I <i>love</i> it.<br /><br />But it does keep me coming back for more. That's the magic of her writing and her stories. I may be getting a little addicted to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6236027800872928945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10947519033756904385" style="display:none">Once you've brained your mortality, salivated about an affair, or lost a loved one, Written on the Body I believe goes from 4 to 5 star worthy, climbs from a tawdry tale to a lovingly wrought prose poem. More contemporary than Graham Greene's The End of the Affair this narrative questions the responsibility of lovers to one another. <br /><br />At the beginning one is certain the narrator female, but by midway testosterone seems to bitterly flavor the advance. However you take this tender sexless narrator (s)he plods the ever onward.<br /><br />The chapters on human anatomy while the narrator is in retreat mode are water for chocolate. <br /><br />The reader is handed the bludgeon of betrayal and the guilt of abandonment while left lightly bubbling in the languor of beer hall pinch-ass to contemplate the role of human existence. The yearning of this novelette is worth getting a bit drunk and crawling under the covers one weekend and caressing to its completion.<br /><br />By the end, even nature isn't much of a solace to the human train wreck.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9845469417803697319">This was a very provocative read for me. There were challenges to what is left of my sense of right and wrong in relationships, there is again that great question of what makes life meaningful and whether one needs another for there to be real meaning in life.   <span id="freeText9845469417803697319" style="display:none">This was a very provocative read for me. There were challenges to what is left of my sense of right and wrong in relationships, there is again that great question of what makes life meaningful and whether one needs another for there to be real meaning in life. Actually, maybe that is not the question the author struggles with - it may be more that real passion in life comes with relationship with another and that respecting that is the real ethic in living. The book ends with several pages of really beautiful writing - prose that flows and rolls and lines that I know I'll want to remember. I did just a few moments ago finish reading the book for the first time - maybe I'll look back later and laugh at myself for being so infatuated, but then again maybe the desire to share life with the intensity that is revealed in this novel will only grow.</span>

<div id="review_17854255" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17854255" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54697-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353271036p2/54697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17854255?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/54697-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=top-shelf">top-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=shattering">shattering</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=femmes">femmes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=fictions-of-the-big-it">fictions-of-the-big-it</a>,
